text:
Awesome flavor, quick and simple to make. I did use 2 cans of basil, garlic and oregano diced tomatoes with their juices instead of fresh tomatoes other than that I followed the recipe. The only reason I gave this a 4 stars is because the sauce was watery, maybe I will use less of the juices and let it reduce before serving. I will definately be making this again.(Update: I did make this again and still used 2 cans of basil, garlic and oregano diced tomatoes but drained the juices from one can and then while cooking I let the sauce reduce until it was thick enough and not watery.)

text:
I love this recipe.  I used fresh garden tomatoes, tripled the garlic,  added dried oregano, and omitted salt.  Because the tomato mixture doesn't really make a sauce, I added 1 cup of white wine and just under a cup of chicken broth.  Let everything simmer and it was simply delicious and light. The grated parmesan cheese is an essential finishing touch.  I will definitely include this dish in my regular rotation.  Thanks!

text:
We like basil, so I put in extra -- probably around 1 1/2 cups. I'll probably use a red pepper flakes, or a sprinkle of cayenne next time.  I think our hot pepper sauce has lost its kick, so this dish didn't have any peppery zip, but the overall flavor was great. I don't think this would have been nearly as good with canned tomatoes, so we will save this recipe and make it again during fresh tomato season. I can also see either substituting shrimp or tofu for the chicken, or leaving it out altogether, for a change of pace.

This was a GREAT recipe..however..from reading the reviews from the other people who had tried it I automatically tried some of their suggestions. I did not use fresh tomatoes but instead used 1can of Italian Seasoned Stewed tomatoes and 1 can of regular diced tomatoes. This recipe is perfect for any "anytime" meal or to impress your most prestiged guests! Thanks Wendy!!!

5 stars with changes: I made a few changes and this turned out so delicious.  I sauteed onions and garlic in olive oil and browned cut up chicken in that.  Then I added chicken broth, a can of diced tomatoes (with oregano, etc) and white wine and the other ingredients (I used 1 tsp crushed pepper instead of hot sauce) and I added some black pepper and a teaspoon of sugar (left fresh basil out until last 10 min).    Then I let it simmer for maybe an hour.  I used mini penne and mixed it all together and topped with shredded parm.   DELICIOUS!

text:
A quick, easy recipe with everyday ingredients that are usually on hand. It based the husband test:)
 Because some viewers said it was bland I seasoned heavily. Since I was preparing for rwo people I used:
  1 piece of boneless breast that I seasoned with garlic/onion powder before browning on stovetop,  2 big garlic cloves, 1/2 med.sized onion, plenty of oregano(per other reviews), easy on the dried basil(no fresh on hand),and two cans of stewed Italian tomatoes with juice. I added pepper, dash of salt, garlic powder, and about 1 teaspoon of sugar(per other reviews).
   I then turned heat up to med. high -covered pot- turned down to med. low and let simmer for about 20 min. I think covering it helped keep it from drying out, as some reviewers complained. Once cooked remove from heat to prevent drying out. It defintely needed the juice from the tomatoes.  Once chicken cooked I stuck it in freezer for a minute so I could shred it a bit (with my hand,nothing fancy). I Added shredded chicken to sauce  and spaghetti until it looked like an even mixture of pasta to sauce. All in all - a 30 min. meal!
Remember - season heavily, use seasoned tomatoes and it'll be a dish to add to your rotation.

text:
Very yummy.  I must admit I made some changes to suit my taste buds, so here they are: Placed in gallon ziploc bag, 4 cubed chicken breasts along with:

2 tbsp italian seasoning
1 tbsp garlic powder
1 tbsp essence of emeril  (recipe on food network)
2 tbsp onion powder
2 tbsp olive oil

Keep all in bag, shaken, in fridge til sauce ready for chicken to be cooked.  First added onions and garlic, let start cooking while chopping 9 roma tomatoes, added, then chopped 1/2 cup fresh basil, then added raw seasoned chicken from gallon bag.  Added 1 cup white wine and put on low/med heat for 5 min to start cooking chicken. Then proceeded with rest of recipe as written. Came out flavorful and very garlicky, but that's a good thing in my book! If you try it, hope you like it!

text:
Not bad. I found this to be a tad bland for my liking (if you are looking for a hearty pasta entree, this is NOT it!), but beyond that, what REALLY stood out to me was the bright, fresh flavors and genius simplicity of this dish. The thermometer nearly reached 90 degrees this weekend. I couldn't have found a better weather-appropriate recipe - not only is this light on the stomach, it's made with seasonally available ingredients and can easily be prepared on the stovetop (thus eliminating the need to use my oven in this heat wave). NOTE: For a nice change of pace, shrimp would be FANTASTIC in this (and a better protein option than chicken, IMHO). Shrimp are delicate, light and fresh and would be a perfect substitute if you have them handy. Just add a crusty loaf of bread and some good wine, and you're are set! All in all, this was yummy, but lacking the WOW factor I was looking for. Thanks anyways, Ms. Mercadante! :-)

text:
Good recipe.  I quartered fresh cherry tomatoes, chopped a large vidalia onion, a whole bunch of green onions (scallions..my fiance loves them), a whole bunch of fresh basil, and about 6 cloves of garlic.  I kept the onions, scallions and garlic together.  I heated the olive oil over medium-high heat, then added the garlic, chopped green onions and the chopped vidalia onion.  Then I added the quartered cherry tomatoes and chopped basil.  I stirred until the tomatoes got soft.    I then threw it into a large bowl that had the pasta already in it.  I then added the hot sauce and mixed everything together with tongs.  I used El Yucateco green hot sauce because it's what I had on hand.  I pretty much followed the recipe to a t but I added a lot more onion than the recipe called for.  I forgot the salt but I don't think it needed it because I did cover our plates with grated Parmesan cheese.  I do recommend using hot sauce, it gives it a great flavor.  Thank you for sharing the recipe Wendy.

EXCELLENT Restaurant Quality meal!!  My family LOVED this recipe (My husband raved about it and my kids, a teenager, a 10 yr old and an 8 yr old, all cleaned their plates). text:
This is an excellent dish.  When I read the reviews I noticed that many of the reviewers who didn't like it, changed the recipe.  You need to be sure and use fresh basil and fresh tomatoes to get the best result.  Also for those who said it was bland, be sure that you have seasoned your chicken before you cook it, if not it will lend to a very bland dish.  I highly recommend.  I did increase the onion and garlic amounts because I know my family prefers more of those flavors but that was done for our taste buds.

text:
3 things bring this up to perfect. 1) be sure to use  2 cans diced tomatoes WITH Basil , Oregano and Garlic, as other reviewers noted. 2) This is much better if you season raw chicken with salt, garlic and herbs like basil and oregano . Then brown  but no need to fully cook. Let it cook the rest if the way in the tomatoes. 3) Either cook down to thicken OR add in a 1t. or so of tomatoe paste, or a small can of tomate sauce 
 I like to pulse the tomates for just a second or 2 till mostly blended
I also stir in FRESH baby spinach. Then top the whole thing with parm cheese and some mozzerella.

This was a light and delicious dish - a really good combination of flavors.  I, per other reviewer suggestions, tinkered with the ingredients a bit:  upped the garlic to 3 cloves, used around 1/2 cup fresh basil, added in some oregano, garlic powder, black pepper, and red pepper flakes.
I didn't have pre-cooked chicken, so I cubed and sauteed the chicken with the onion and garlic (and spices) until cooked, added in the chopped tomatoes and a little bit of chicken stock to make is "sauce-y"  Simmered for 15-20 minutes and everything was delicious!  A nice little kick from the hot sauce (used a habanero sauce) and wonderful fresh flavors.  Will definitely make again

Very tasty and healthy! We used Tofu Shiratake  noodles (20 cal. .5 fat per serving!).. I tweaked it a little to add more flavor since the noodles can be a bit bland.

1st, marinated the chicken over night in Olive oil, basil, garlic, & seasonings to taste.

2nd, Used one large fresh tomato chopped and used a half can of petite diced tomatoes. 

3rd, In the last few minutes of cooking, I added the Shiratake Tofu noodles to absorb some flavor.

Turned out great! My fiance couldn't even tell there were tofu noodles involved!

text:
Good basic recipe that is outstanding with a few tweaks...

I doubled the ingredients and made a big batch as I like to eat it all week long.  For the doubled batch, I use 4 large chicken breasts(about 2 pounds worth) that I grill with Italian Seasoning.  I double, if not triple the garlic.  Fresh ingredients are key.  Fresh tomatoes, fresh garlic, fresh basil, fresh parmesan make this dish killer!

My "secret" is to add a diced red bell pepper and about half a pound of white mushrooms to the sauce.

When making the sauce, I add a healthy splash of red wine to the mixture and cook for an additional 3-5 minutes to make it slightly more "saucy" and let the tomatoes become very tender.

Plate and top with a shower of fresh parmesan... DELICIOUS!

text:
Alright, so I am going to start off by saying that I messed up on this. I made too much pasta (I used a 16 oz. box on accident. Good thing I didn't do the box and a half it called for.) and I chopped the onions too finely in an electric chopper. I almost put an entire bulb of garlic into the dish too, good thing Karen was there to stop me. A couple of things that I wish I would have done for this recipe. I wish I would have heated up the pan before I put the oil in there to start sautÃ©ing the onions. I wish I would have started chopping everything a little earlier. Instead of 15 minute prep time, I would have given myself 30 - 40 minutes. But I am by no means an experienced cook. So people who actually know how to chop things can give themselves less time. Lastly, I would have made sure the tomatoes were a little fresher. Ours were a little mushy by the time everything was finished.  Some things we are considering doing the next time include adding a bit more hot sauce to give it a little kick and not tossing it all together so the chicken and tomatoes don't go all to the bottom. That way everyone get some as opposed to digging in the bottom to get the chicken out. Overall this was a really good recipe. Everyone at the dinner table loved it, including myself. If I wouldn't have had so much to eat at lunch, I definitely would have put a second helping on my plate.

text:
Excellent recipe!  A few suggestions:
1.  Use a short pasta - ziti, penne, rigatoni, etc.  The sauce is thin and slides ride off the angel hair so you have several bites of either just pasta or just sauce.  With the shorter pasta you get both in one bite.
2.  Top with more fresh basil (or sage or oregano or all three)
3.  Double the garlic

text:
This was AMAZING. My fiance LOVED IT. I left out the hot petter sauce because we're not huge on spicy food. I also added a 1.5 tsp of sugar and 1 tsp of balsamic vinegar to deglaze the pan after sauteing the onions and garlic. I find that tomato skins kind of get in the way and get stuck in your teeth so I stick my tomatoes in boiling water for 40 seconds and then dunk them in ice water and the sin comes right off and you get lovely lush tomatoes. Don't be afraid to use more basil! 

One thing I didn't like about this recipe was that it calls for the basil to be put in very early on in the cooking which really kills the flavor of the basil. Put it in at the last minute and you'll notice a stark difference and a huge burst of flavor.

text:
Excellent recipe, but I gave it 4 stars instead of 5 because I did make changes based on the suggestions of previous reviewers: 1. Instead of the chopped tomatoes, I used 2 cans of Del Monte Diced Tomatoes w/ basil, garlic & oregano flavor. 2. I used a basil paste (sold in small tubes in the tofu section) because that was all I had at home. 3. Omitted the hot pepper sauce as my family does not like anything spicy. 4. Added 3 oz. (1/2 can) tomato paste to thicken the sauce. 5. Added 1/2 teaspoon sugar. 6. Added a splash of white wine to the onion and garlic saute. Great base recipe that you can add or remove ingredients to suit your taste. Will definitely make again!

My family enjoyed this dish. I used 4 raw chicken breast cut up in chunks, cooked them with 1 chopped onion, 2 rounded tbsp of minced garlic, dried basil, salt, pepper and a dash of red pepper flakes. Once the chicken was almost fully cooked I then added the tomatoes. I used 2 fresh and 1 can of diced because I didn't have enough fresh on hand. text:
Honestly, I've been making a similar recipe since back in the 1980's (yikes -- dating myself, here), reminiscent of California Pizza Kitchen (where it is no longer on the menu), and have been making it ever since then, just guessing on ingredients and throwing it all together.  But this is the first recipe I've seen that actually has a recipe, measures out the ingredients, and pretty much guarantees that it will always come out about the same whenever you make it.  I love the mix of ingredients in this recipe, and the chicken really tops it off.  True family fare, and great "comfort food," too.  

I'll add that I no longer buy commercial-brand pasta sauce, because this is my FAVORITE, and when I want angel hair pasta, this is what I want.

I've made this with both parboiled fresh tomatoes and also by simply opening a can of diced tomatoes, due to time constraints, and also with and without mushrooms, fresh or canned (yum!).

Anyway, this is super quick as either a side or a main dish, and I highly recommend it!

text:
I made this for dinner tonight and it was wonderful! I seasoned it to my taste ignoring the spices the recipe called for. I chopped up a clove of garlic, 4 Roma tomatoes, a red onion, green bell pepper, red bell pepper, and one bunch of green onions, sautÃ©ed all of the above in olive oil and seasoned with garlic salt, a pinch of table salt, Badia Cajun seasoning, crushed red pepper flakes, basil, and a little cayenne. SautÃ©ed it until it was soft, then slowly stirred in my wheat linguini pasta I had boiled. I mixed the pasta into the pan so that the pasta could absorb all of the seasonings on the bottom of the saucepan. While that was sitting, I seasoned the chicken breasts separately, this is important so that the chicken will have its own distinct flavor to add to the dish. In a separate pan I sliced yellow onions and sautÃ©ed them in olive oil seasoned with only garlic salt. Btw I seasoned the chicken with Badia complete seasoning and garlic salt. Once the yellow onions were browning I added the breasts and let them cook on both sides, before removing them from the pan I sliced the breasts into strips and let them cook a minute longer, then I poured the whole contents over the pasta and mixed them up. Fantastic meal! Yes it was a lot of work but worth it in the end. Other reviewers complained about not having enough sauce, the key is to use enough olive oil, it's healthy and coats the pasta well. Steamed some broccoli as a side dish and garlic bread. Yummy.

text:
This went over pretty well with the family.  I used grape tomatoes sliced in half so the tomatoes didn't get really limp.  I also used chili flakes rather than the hot pepper sauce.  In these types of dishes that include cooked chicen I have found that poorly prepared chicken can negatively affect the outcome of the dish.  For this one, I cubed the chicken raw and put it in a resealable bag along with about a tablespoon of oil.  Shook the bag to coat the chicken and then poured in a package of McCormick's Sweet Basil & Oregano Bruschetta Chicken seasoning.  Spread it on a baking sheet and cooked at 350 degrees for about 12 minutes. Made the rest of the dish as the recipe indicated.  Will be making this again.

I usually try not to review a recipe I deviate too far from, but I used this as a base and came up with something good, so I want to give this recipe credit.  I had left over heavy cream and fresh basil from making "Rich and Creamy Tomato Basil Soup" from this site, so I used this recipe and those ingredients to make a hybrid meal.  I cooked tomatoes, chicken, fresh basil, heavy cream, and a can of chicken broth  then poured it over the angel hair.  With the chicken and the heavy cream the soup/sauce really holds up.  This recipe is a nice change from sauce heavy pastas.

text:
As written it's a good recipe.  I didn't really change anything except to add more garlic and use canned tomatoes instead of fresh.  Like others I like my sauces a little thicker and the canned tomatoes are just too watery on their own.  I added tomato paste to thicken it up.  Also, because I didn't have cooked chicken leftover, I browned chicken in a skillet, took it out and added the onions and garlic and softened them then added the chicken, tomatoes and other ingredients in.  So I essentially made it a one pot dish minus the pasta.  Overall, really good fast meal!

This is such a fantastic pasta! I just love that it is healthy, too! I used whole wheat angel hair pasta for additional healthiness, and that worked really well. I used a 14.5oz can of diced tomatoes with basil, garlic, and oregano seasonings. That worked perfectly! I drained half of the juice from the can. The remaining really helped to coat the pasta when I added it to the sauce. Other reviewers said they thought the canned wasn't as good as fresh tomatoes, but I think it would be just as good if not better. Less work, too! I also added canned mushrooms. Served this with salad and garlic toast. I'll definately be making this again and again!!

I made this last week, it was just for my brother and I but my Dad who doesn't like chicken or pasta got a whiff of it and wanted it as well. I didn't have any angel hair pasta so I just used twists. I read a review where someone said marinade the chicken first so I did. I put it in with oil lemon herbs tobasco and garlic. I used a bit more tomato than was called for but just let it simmer for longer and reduce to make a thicker sauce. There was a lovely kick to this recipe and I would reccomend this to anyone. I used all dried herbs and it was fine. Made the house smell lovely and all I kept hearing was "is it ready yet? It smells gorgeous." Just give it a try it is well worth it.
